### Ze Dude (@ZeDude1510)
_Sun Jul 12 15:53:09 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/ZeDude1510/status/2076334054924836978)

> J’ai essayé de faire une synthèse de ce qui se passe dans le domaine des Semi ces dernières semaines et pourquoi c’est aussi volatile :
>
> 1. le CPO prendrait plus de temps que prévu :
> Le scale-up CPO (optique intégrée au plus près des GPU) serait repoussé. Le véritable ramp pourrait finalement intervenir fin 2028 / 2029 plutôt qu'en 2027.
>
> Les principales raisons évoquées :
> difficultés      de fabrication,
> rendements      insuffisants,
> packaging      complexe,
> coûts      encore trop élevés.
>
> MAIS attention, ca ne signifie pas que la photonique est morte
>
> Au contraire, cela prolonge la durée de vie de :
> 800G,
> 1.6T      pluggables,
> LPO,
> NPO,
> CW      lasers,
> cuivre      actif (AEC).
>
> Petit parenthèse pour Sivers : 
> Même si le gros ramp est repoussé de quelques trimestres, cela laisse justement plus de temps à Sivers pour :
> augmenter      sa capacité de production,
> améliorer      les rendements,
> obtenir      les qualifications,
> signer de      nouveaux contrats,
> sécuriser      davantage de clients.
>
> Les hyperscalers ne vont pas attendre 2028 pour commencer à qualifier leurs fournisseurs.
>
> Les capacités industrielles doivent être prêtes avant les volumes.
> À mon sens, cela n'empêche absolument pas de voir de nombreuses bonnes nouvelles en 2026-2027.
>  Mais comme d’hab, l’exécution doit suivre
>
> 2. Rumeurs de retard Rubin
> Plusieurs rumeurs évoquaient un retard de Rubin.
>
> À ce stade :
> aucune      confirmation officielle,
> Nvidia      continue de communiquer normalement,
> plusieurs      sources ont contesté ces rumeurs.
> Prudence donc avant de considérer un retard majeur comme acquis.
>
> 3 .Rapport B. Riley sur AAOI
> B. Riley estime que les nouvelles architectures réseau (Amazon RNG, OpenAI MRC) pourraient réduire le nombre de liens optiques nécessaires.
> Leur scénario :
> moins de      switches,
> moins de      transceivers,
> donc      moins de demande pour des sociétés comme AAOI.
> C'est probablement la note la plus baissière de la semaine.
>  MAIS cela a été contredit par de nombreuses personnes :
>
> On a vu : Rosenblatt , Goldman Sachs,  Morgan Stanley,  Photon Capital,  plusieurs anciens ingénieurs réseaux dire à peu près : 
> oui les architectures évoluent, mais non cela ne détruit pas la demande optique.
>  Pourquoi ? Parce que B.Riley raisonne surtout sur  nombre de liens.
> Les autres répondent : oui, mais :
> les liens      deviennent beaucoup plus rapides
> plus chers , plus  complexes ,plus de contenu optique
> plus de coherent  , plus de  lasers , plus de DSP ,plus de CW lasers
>
> Donc le nombre de ports peut diminuer...sans que le chiffre d'affaires du secteur baisse.
>
> Maintenant pour les nouvelles positives :
> Goldman Sachs
> Continue de voir :
> Optical Devices : Very Tight
> Optical Cables : Very Tight
> jusqu'en 2027.
> Autrement dit :
> malgré toutes les nouvelles capacités de production, la demande resterait supérieure à l'offre.
>
> Rosenblatt , on l'a vu reste très positif sur AAOI en particulier 
> Reste très positif.
> Ils continuent notamment d'anticiper pour AAOI :
> Beat
> Raise
> Guidance Q3 proche de 300 M$
> Ils considèrent que les vendeurs à découvert exploitent surtout la peur actuelle.
>
> Morgan Stanley
> Morgan Stanley reste positif sur le thème IA.
> Ils mettent surtout en avant les véritables bottlenecks 
> mémoire,
> énergie,
> photonique,
> interconnexions,
> power delivery.

### Alex A.C. (@AnalysisOp)
_Sun Jul 12 16:54:45 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 11 · ↻ 3 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/AnalysisOp/status/2076349554249666628)

> Fren Photon Capital about the "battle" CPO ⚔️ Transceivers:
>
> "Rather than CPO replacing every pluggable, form factors like pluggables, LPO, and CPO are likely to coexist depending on distance and power budget. [For example] NVIDIA is growing its CPO switches and its pluggable ecosystem side by side"
>
> Yes, the CPO growth will be explosive, but the CAGR of the Transceivers will be there to compound for you, don't forget it. 
> About the concept of "power budget", I'm more inclined to think it's a concept of COOLING. Even having "free energy" you can't put together a lot of non-CPO photonics connections in high density.
>
> 'Photonics' it's not a monolithic thing; it exists different layers inside the chips:
>
> "Switch CPO and XPU-HBM Optical I/O Are Different Contests. Two adjacent architectures often grouped under the CPO and optical-I/O umbrella must be kept apart.
>
> And I add: switch CPO for scale-up is also a different contest than CPO for scale-out and scale-across. That's why Transceivers are also here to stay with us.

### Kai - Briefing Block (@briefing_block_)
_Sun Jul 12 22:00:02 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 2 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/briefing_block_/status/2076426381123326169)

> $MRVL  Is Building the Physical AI Stack Around the GPU
>
> Data-center revenue hit $1.83B in fiscal Q1, or 76% of sales.
>
> The bigger signal is how many AI bottlenecks Marvell can monetize as the cluster becomes a systems problem.
>
> The architecture
>
> Marvell starts with custom AI accelerators and XPU-related silicon.
>
> It then moves into the plumbing that determines whether those chips run at useful utilization.
>
> That includes electro-optical DSPs, 800G and 1.6T links, Ethernet switches and storage controllers.
>
> It also covers scale-up networking within and beyond racks, scale-out fabrics between racks, and long-distance data-center interconnect.
>
> Marvell can therefore sell into compute, XPU attach, optical conversion, switching, storage, and the links between data centers.
>
> Calling that “full stack” is generous because Marvell does not own the software layer, but its physical footprint is increasingly broad.
>
> That breadth matters because more accelerators do not remove bandwidth, latency, power, or memory-access constraints.
>
> They make the cost of those constraints harder to ignore.
>
> The second-order trade
>
> The real question is not “GPUs versus networking.”
>
> It is whether spending around each accelerator rises as clusters become larger and less tolerant of idle compute.
>
> The latest numbers support that read.
>
> Q1 revenue grew 28%, while management guided Q2 revenue to roughly $2.7B.
>
> Management cited strength across 800G and 1.6T optics, 51.2T Ethernet switches, scale-up optics, DCI modules and custom XPU solutions.
>
> Marvell is also sampling a 102.4 Tbps Teralynx switch designed for both scale-out and scale-up fabrics.
>
> NVIDIA’s $2B preferred investment adds validation, but the strategic value is integration with NVLink Fusion and joint silicon-photonics work.
>
> The catch
>
> This is not a risk-free picks-and-shovels story.
>
> Custom programs are concentrated, qualification cycles are long, and one delayed hyperscaler ramp can hit revenue and the multiple.
>
> Three customers represented roughly 75% of gross receivables.
>
> A broader product stack does not yet mean a broadly diversified customer base.
>
> At roughly 20x annualized Q2 revenue, the market is already paying for platform-level execution.
>
> Bottom line: Marvell is becoming a multi-layer AI infrastructure supplier, but the stock already assumes those layers scale on time and together.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HNCTrk1aQAADsYx.jpg

### Stanford U Huff Post (@Tyroist)
_Thu Jul 09 19:05:06 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Tyroist/status/2075295194011041864)

> Creating more energy?
> Binary is on or off which takes power to turn on or off.
> The most power is consumed when the bit changes state (e.g., flipping from a 0 to a 1).
>
> Is there a lower power way to change state? Like colors or a state change in a lower temp environment?
>
> AI:
> Yes, there are much lower-power ways to change a bit's state, and your intuition about using colors and lower temperature environments is spot on with cutting-edge physics and computer engineering.
> Modern computers waste a massive amount of energy pushing whole streams of electrons through wires. To bypass this, researchers are developing alternatives based exactly on the concepts you mentioned:
> 1. Lower Temperature Environments (The Physics Proof)
> In physics, there is an absolute fundamental limit to how cheap a state change can be, called the Landauer's principle.
> Why temperature matters: Notice the T(temperature) in the equation. Because temperature is directly multiplied by the energy cost, dropping the temperature drastically lowers the minimum energy required to flip a bit. In ultra-cold quantum computing or superconducting environments, the thermal "noise" is so low that bits can change state with a fraction of the energy required at room temperature.
>
> 2. Using Colors and Light (Photonics)
> Instead of forcing electrons through a silicon transistor, scientists use Optical and Photonic Computing, which relies on light (colors/wavelengths).
> Optical Switches: Instead of charging a capacitor with electricity, a pulse of light switches a material between being transparent or reflective.
> The Power Advantage: Photons (light particles) do not have mass or electrical charge, meaning they do not generate heat through electrical resistance. Using different wavelengths (colors) allows data states to change at the speed of light with almost zero energy loss. Recent breakthroughs include devices combining magnetism with light to switch states in picoseconds using orders of magnitude less power than traditional electronics.
> 3. Structural State Changes (Phase-Change & Magnetics)
> Beyond light and cold, there are structural ways to rewrite data using minimal energy:
> Spintronics (Magnetic Bits): Instead of moving electrons from point A to point B, you simply change the spin (magnetic direction) of an electron right where it sits. This uses almost no moving current and has no capacitive electrical loss.
> Phase-Change Memory (PCM): This approach mimics your idea of a physical state change. A tiny electrical pulse switches a glass-like material between an amorphous state (disorganized atoms = 0) and a crystalline state (organized atoms = 1). Once changed, it stays in that state forever without requiring any holding power.

### Tech Equity Engineer (@TechEquityEng)
_Thu Jul 09 19:33:50 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 33 · ↻ 3 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/TechEquityEng/status/2075302426404389326)

> I spent some time reading $AUR latest engineering blog, and one thing really stood out to me.
>
> They’ve built a custom silicon photonic engine for their FirstLight lidar, consolidating light generation, amplification, and detection into a compact multi-chip module.
>
> I don’t think enough people appreciate how important this hardware moat is.
> Getting autonomous driving software to work is only half the battle. You have to build hardware that is repeatable, reliable, and cost-effective enough to deploy at scale.
>
> A few key takeaways:
> • Fiber-free architecture: They eliminated fragile fiber connectors entirely, routing light through integrated waveguides to survive heavy-duty truck vibrations over hundreds of thousands of miles.
>
> • Automated sub-micron assembly: Instead of slow, manual lab calibration, they use automated active alignment to position microlenses between chips in real-time on the production line.
>
> • Vertical stack ownership: They design everything in-house, down to the epitaxial layers of their lasers, giving them total control over the automotive qualification process (PPAP) and allowing rapid architectural iteration.
>
> As an investor, this is the stuff I pay attention to.
>
> The AI gets all the headlines, but deep hardware engineering decisions like these determine whether a company can actually scale from hundreds of vehicles to tens of thousands.
>
> This is another reason I’m bullish on $AUR and it continues to be my highest conviction moonshot play for the next decade. 
>
> -T.E.E.

### JSCC (@JSCC2020Lee)
_Thu Jul 09 21:23:59 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/JSCC2020Lee/status/2075330145507049472)

> **July 9-10, 2026 | CPO & Photonics Daily Update**
>
> CPO momentum stays constructive as the AI data center supply chain builds supporting infrastructure for the optics transition. No major new product launches broke yesterday, but clear signals emerged from upstream players that demand for CPO-related services and analysis is rising in lockstep with hyperscaler deployment plans.
>
> **Overall Sector View**  
> The shift from copper to co-packaged optics continues to advance as a structural necessity for power efficiency and bandwidth scaling in AI factories. NVIDIA and Broadcom remain the primary platform drivers, with TSMC’s advanced packaging technologies (COUPE and related nodes) providing critical manufacturing backbone. Recent volatility in optics stocks appears more sentiment-driven than fundamental, as long-term visibility on 2026-2027 ramps remains intact.
>
> **Key Development**  
> Taiwanese material and failure analysis leaders MA-tek and Msscorps posted record Q2 revenues. Growth was fueled by surging demand for advanced process, silicon photonics, and CPO-related services. Both companies highlighted CPO analysis as a high-ASP, customized growth driver and are investing in new equipment to support yield improvement and faster time-to-market for optical-AI chip integration. This reflects tangible ecosystem maturation ahead of broader CPO adoption.
>
> **Major Players Snapshot**  
> • **NVIDIA (NVDA)**: Execution on Spectrum-X and Quantum-X CPO platforms continues. Earlier shipments of TSMC-backed switches point to H2 2026 volume ramp-up targeting interconnect and power bottlenecks in large AI clusters.  
> • **TSMC (TSM)**: Central foundry and packaging enabler. Rising demand for CPO-related analysis and production support underscores its strategic position in the photonics supply chain.  
> • **Broadcom (AVGO)**: Tomahawk 6 / Bailly CPO platform serves as a key Ethernet benchmark. Vertical integration and ecosystem partnerships help address reliability and scaling requirements.
>
> **Supply Chain & Optics Players**  
> LITE, COHR, and AAOI continue to track AI infrastructure cycles, with component demand (lasers, engines, interconnects) supporting structural growth. Taiwanese specialists (FOCI/3363, ShunSin/6451) and SIVE benefit indirectly through increased testing, analysis, and packaging activity. Recent moves by analysis providers signal that upstream readiness for higher-volume CPO deployments in switches — and eventual GPU-scale integration — is progressing.
>
> **Core CPO Takeaways**  
> • CPO adoption path is methodical: early scale-out switch deployments in 2026, followed by scale-up optical I/O ramps later in the decade. Power savings, density gains, and reduced laser count remain the primary value drivers.  
> • Supporting ecosystem (packaging, testing, lasers, analysis) is expanding in parallel, helping de-risk supply chain bottlenecks for hyperscalers.
>
> CPO remains a multi-year structural theme in AI infrastructure. Watch for continued execution signals from platform leaders and incremental supply chain expansions as 2026 volume targets approach. Long-term visibility favors companies enabling the optics transition across the full stack.
>
> #CPO #CoPackagedOptics #AIInfrastructure #Photonics #Semiconductors

> On Serenity: No one has to blindly follow every pick. The $SIVE thesis doesn’t stand or fall with one person - it stands on the partners and supply chain reality.
>
> Bonus context today: 
> While one former executive sold, the people with the best information bought into the dip:
> > Board member Todd Thomson (ex-Citigroup CFO) bought 535k SEK at 42.80 SEK
> > Board member Karin Raj bought 460k SEK at the intraday low (34.68 SEK)
> > CEO Vikram Vathulya acquired ~1M SEK
>
> All reported same day. These are the same people who approved the Q-report clarifications and Nasdaq listing process.
>
> If execution comes, the numbers will matter more than any single sale or the last 10 picks.
>
> Stay skeptical. But don’t reduce everything to „just hype“ when real design-ins, reference designs, and insider buying from key board members already exist.

>
> With lots of the focus on lasers/transceivers.
>
> My goal with this post isn't to refute that.
>
> We can talk about how much demand is still showing up
>
> Or the difference between 'capacity' and 'qualified capacity'
>
> Or the different moats that exist for certain porducts.
>
> And more. But I won't dig into that now.
>
> For those of you that are concerned about oversupply at these layers, I want to encourage you...
>
> Don't look at the Photonics sector as 1 general trade.
>
> While they generally share sentiment and move in sync, the different layers have different headwinds & tailwinds. 
>
> Hopefully different companies will be albe to de-sync and the most durable will outperform.
>
> Sure, the market can decide it doesn't want to reward a premium multiple. Fine. 
>
> Let's separate the stock from the company for a sec. 
>
> Think about it....
>
> Which companies will BENEFIT if there is an eventual oversupply at the laser/transceiver level?
>
> > Does more volume here mean more fiber deployment from $GLW ? 
>
> > Does more laser supply/availability mean that $NOK $CIEN can better meet their demand?
>
> > Does more volume mean more components that need to get tested? $AEHR $FORM $VIAV 
>
> Would love to hear your thoughts around who would be hurt and who would benefit. 
>
> Assuming that supply does actually catch up to demand at any near point.

### GUL (@gulVasikova)
_Wed Jul 08 18:04:13 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 2 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/gulVasikova/status/2074917486324314306)

> 🇨🇦 Canada is quietly becoming one of the world’s biggest quantum computing hubs, and investors are starting to pay attention.
>
> For years, Canada invested heavily in quantum research while much of the market focused on AI. Now that companies like $NVDA are openly embracing quantum computing, investors are beginning to realize that Canada may already have one of the strongest quantum ecosystems outside the U.S.
>
> Since 2002, Canada has invested more than $2 billion into quantum technology, while the government recently committed another $334 million to accelerate development. That funding isn’t just supporting research—it’s helping build an entire industry spanning hardware, software, cybersecurity, networking, and future AI infrastructure.
>
> One of the biggest names is $XNDU (Xanadu Quantum Technologies), which recently became Canada’s first publicly traded pure-play quantum computing company.
>
> Unlike many competitors building superconducting quantum computers, Xanadu is developing photonic quantum computers, which use light (photons) instead of electrical circuits. Many researchers believe photonics could eventually offer better scalability, lower cooling requirements, and easier integration into future AI data centers.
>
> Canada’s strength extends well beyond one company.
>
> Companies like $BTQ, Quantum eMotion, Photonic, Nord Quantique, and Quantum Technologies are all building different pieces of the future quantum ecosystem, from post-quantum cybersecurity to fault-tolerant quantum hardware.
>
> A major validation came when DARPA, the U.S. Defense Advanced Research Projects Agency, selected several Canadian quantum startups for its Quantum Benchmarking Initiative. DARPA is looking for technologies capable of building commercially useful quantum computers by 2033.
>
> That recognition suggests Canadian companies are competing on a global stage—not just in academic research.
>
> Why is $XNDU heavily shorted?
>
> Despite the excitement, $XNDU currently has one of the highest short interests in the market, with over 70% of its free float sold short.
>
> Short sellers believe the company’s valuation has moved far ahead of today’s business fundamentals. Revenue remains relatively small, profitability is still years away, and commercial quantum computing is still in its early stages.
>
> Their argument is simple:
>
> “The technology is promising—but investors may be paying tomorrow’s price for a company that is still building today’s products.”
>
> However, the opposite argument is equally compelling.
>
> If $XNDU continues hitting technical milestones, signs major commercial partnerships, or demonstrates meaningful progress toward scalable quantum computing, that extremely high short interest could fuel a powerful short squeeze, forcing bearish investors to buy back shares at much higher prices.
>
> Wall Street remains constructive despite the volatility, with analysts maintaining a Moderate Buy rating and an average price target implying roughly 275% upside from recent trading levels.
>
> The bigger picture
>
> Think about AI 15 years ago.
>
> Back then, most AI companies generated little revenue and many looked expensive. Investors who focused only on current earnings often missed the enormous opportunity that followed.
>
> Quantum computing could be following a similar path.
>
> Today it’s still experimental.
>
> Over the next decade, it could transform drug discovery, financial modeling, materials science, cybersecurity, climate simulation, and AI itself.
>
> There will likely be winners and losers along the way, but Canada has quietly positioned itself as one of the global leaders in this race.
>
> For long-term investors, the real question isn’t whether quantum computing will matter.
>
> It’s which companies will become the Nvidia, TSMC, or Microsoft of the quantum era. $XNDU is one of the companies trying to earn that position, making it one of the more closely watched—and most controversial—quantum stocks in the market today.

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HMuWdF9awAAW5gk.jpg

### 투자/주식의 생활화 퇴직 오과장 (@datastaion)
_Wed Jul 08 18:45:37 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 5 · ↻ 0 · 💬 1 · [open on X](https://x.com/datastaion/status/2074927905860427952)

> AI 사이클 내년이후로 길게보면
> 엔비디아 TSMC 브로드컴
> 지표기업들
> 컴퓨팅파워와 속도 네트워킹.
> ㅡㅡㅡㅡㅡ
>
> [뉴스] TSMC의 PIC 생산 능력, 2028년까지 월 25,000장으로 급증 전망; 엔비디아와 브로드컴이 초기 COUPE 고객으로 거론됨
>
> TSMC가 실리콘 포토닉스(Silicon Photonics) 분야로 사업을 확장하면서 시장의 관심이 쏠리고 있는 가운데, PIC(광집적회로, Photonic Integrated Circuits) 웨이퍼 생산 능력이 대폭 확대될 것으로 예상됩니다. 상업시보(Commercial Times)에 따르면, 기관 투자자들은 TSMC의 PIC 생산 능력이 월 약 500장 수준에서 2026년 2분기 10,000장으로 늘어나고, 4분기에는 15,000장으로 추가 확대되며, 2028년에는 월 최소 25,000장에 달할 것으로 추산하고 있습니다.
>
> 해당 보도에서 강조했듯, 초기 생산 램프업(생산량 확대) 기간 동안에는 PIC 생산 능력이 제한적이기 때문에 2026~2027년 TSMC의 COUPE 플랫폼 양산을 이용할 주요 고객은 엔비디아(NVIDIA), 브로드컴(Broadcom), AMD가 될 가능성이 높습니다. 2028년에 생산 능력이 더욱 확대되면, 미디어텍(MediaTek), 마벨(Marvell), 아야 랩스(Ayar Labs) 등 고객사의 CPO(공동 패키지 광학, Co-Packaged Optics) 프로젝트 역시 TSMC의 양산 플랫폼에 진입할 수 있을 것으로 보입니다.
>
> PIC는 전기 및 광 신호를 변환, 라우팅, 결합하는 역할을 담당합니다. AI 서버 클러스터가 지속적으로 확장되고 스위치 대역폭이 25T 및 50T에서 100T 및 200T로 고도화됨에 따라 광 엔진에 대한 수요도 증가하고 있으며, 이에 따라 TSMC의 COUPE 플랫폼 진행 상황이 시장의 주요 관심사가 되고 있다고 보도는 덧붙였습니다.
>
> 이 보도에 따르면, 웨이퍼당 648개의 다이(die)가 생산된다고 가정할 때, TSMC의 월간 PIC 생산 능력이 500장에서 10,000장으로 늘어나면 연간 PIC 생산량은 약 400만 개에서 7,800만 개로 급증하게 됩니다. 생산 능력이 월 25,000장으로 더욱 확대될 경우, 연간 PIC 생산량은 약 1억 9,400만 개에 달할 수 있습니다.
>
> 이러한 전망을 바탕으로, 해당 보도는 TSMC의 PIC 생산 능력 확대가 갖는 세 가지 주요 시사점을 강조합니다.
>
> 1. CPO의 양산 진입: 
> CPO 기술이 실험 및 소량 검증 단계를 넘어 점차 대량 생산 준비 단계로 나아가고 있음을 의미합니다.
>
> 2. 포괄적 AI 플랫폼 구축: 
> 실리콘 포토닉스와 첨단 패키징(Advanced Packaging)의 결합을 통해 COUPE, SoIC, CoWoS를 모두 결합한 더욱 포괄적인 AI 광전(optoelectronic) 플랫폼이 구축될 것으로 예상됩니다.
>
> 3. 관련 장비 수요 증가: 
> PIC 생산량이 증가함에 따라 광섬유 어레이 유닛(FAU), 레이저, 광학 테스트 장비, 프로브 카드(Probe cards), 테스트 소켓 및 자동화 장비에 대한 수요를 견인할 것으로 예상됩니다.
>
> 상용화를 향해 나아가는 TSMC의 COUPE 플랫폼
> 경제일보(Economic Daily News)의 보도처럼, TSMC는 자사의 COUPE 플랫폼을 기반으로 한 세계 최초의 200Gbps 마이크로 링 변조기(MRM, Micro-Ring Modulator)가 2026년 하반기에 양산에 들어갈 예정이라고 발표했습니다. 
> 또한 TSMC는 이 소자가 공정 제어 조건 하에서 1E-08 미만의 비트 에러율(Bit Error Rate)을 달성했다고 밝혔습니다.
>
> 그러나 상업시보는 PIC 생산 능력 증가가 곧바로 CPO의 대규모 양산 램프업을 의미하는 것은 아니라고 지적합니다. 
>
> 다운스트림(후공정) 프로세스가 완성되기 위해서는 SoIC 통합, 광전 테스트, 광 엔진 패키징, FAU 결합, 시스템 수준의 검증 등 여러 단계를 아직 통과해야 하기 때문입니다.
>
> https://t.co/w4FQ8IuzkB

### Jakub Kostrzewa, CFA, DI (@_JakubKostrzewa)
_Wed Jul 08 19:13:45 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 16 · ↻ 1 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/_JakubKostrzewa/status/2074934983177785689)

> Wieczorne podsumowanie rynków | 08.07.2026 📈📉
>
> Środa była dniem powrotu geopolityki na pierwszy plan. Donald Trump ogłosił, że porozumienie z Iranem jest skończone, ropa wystrzeliła, rentowności amerykańskich obligacji poszły w górę, a inwestorzy znów zaczęli liczyć potencjalne koszty konfliktu w rejonie Cieśniny Ormuz 🛢️⚠️.
>
> Na tym tle GPW wypadła zaskakująco dobrze. WIG20 w ciągu dnia tracił prawie 2%, ale finalnie zakończył sesję niemal na zero. Warszawa dostała cios z zewnątrz, ale nie położyła się na deskach 🇵🇱🥊.
>
> 🇵🇱 GPW: Duża nerwowość, mała zmiana na zamknięciu 🦅
> Na zamknięciu WIG20 spadł symbolicznie o 0,05%, szeroki WIG stracił 0,06%, a sWIG80 zniżkował o 0,47%. Najlepiej zachował się mWIG40, który wzrósł o 0,23%.
>
> Obroty były wysokie i wyniosły 2,45 mld zł, z czego ponad 2 mld zł przypadło na WIG20. Największy handel koncentrował się na KGHM, Allegro, Orlenie i PKO BP. To była sesja dużych spółek i dużych emocji 💰.
>
> Orlen korzysta z drogiej ropy: Liderem WIG20 został Orlen (+3,51%). Skok cen ropy natychmiast poprawił sentyment do paliwowego giganta. W tle inwestorzy wyceniali ryzyko kolejnych problemów z transportem surowca przez Cieśninę Ormuz ⛽📈.
>
> Banki pomagają indeksowi: Dobrze wyglądały też Alior (+1,38%), Pekao (+1,34%) i PKO BP (+1,22%). To ważne, bo dziś RPP zgodnie z oczekiwaniami utrzymała stopy procentowe bez zmian, ze stopą referencyjną na poziomie 3,75%. Rynek dostał więc pauzę, a nie zaskoczenie 🏦.
>
> Allegro i Dino po zielonej stronie: W drugiej części sesji popyt pojawił się także na Allegro (+0,76%) i Dino (+0,80%). To pomogło WIG20 ograniczyć skalę spadku, mimo mocnej przeceny kilku ciężkich komponentów indeksu 🛒.
>
> KGHM głównym hamulcem: Największym problemem GPW był dziś KGHM (-6,69%). Spółce ciążyły spadki miedzi i srebra, a inwestorzy nadal trawią nową strategię 2055+. Rynek coraz uważniej patrzy na możliwe wyższe nakłady inwestycyjne i potencjalne transakcje M&A ⛏️📉.
>
> Budimex i przemysł pod presją: Słabo wypadł Budimex (-3,70%), a pod kreską znalazły się też Kęty (-1,74%) i Modivo (-1,49%). Bez wsparcia Orlenu i banków WIG20 wyglądałby dziś znacznie gorzej.
>
> Szeroki rynek z kilkoma mocnymi historiami: W mWIG40 świetnie poradziły sobie Inter Cars (+5,50%), Creotech (+4,56%) i Text (+4,21%). Creotech pomógł pozytywny komunikat o uzyskaniu łączności z satelitą Mikroglob-1, a Text kontynuował dobrą passę po wcześniejszych pozytywnych impulsach analitycznych 🚀.
>
> Po słabszej stronie znalazły się Polimex Mostostal (-4,96%), Lubawa (-3,94%), Rainbow (-3,66%) i Ten Square Games (-3,50%). W sWIG80 uwagę przyciągał Huuuge (-3,64%) po słabszych danych o przychodach za II kwartał, a pozytywnie wyróżniło się VIGO Photonics (+1,85%) po rekordowych kwartalnych przychodach.
>
> 🇺🇸 Wall Street: Ropa straszy Dow, chipy ratują Nasdaq 🇺🇸
> Za oceanem nastroje były nerwowe. Dow Jones tracił ponad 1%, S&P 500 był pod kreską, a Nasdaq zdołał odrobić część strat i krążył blisko poziomu odniesienia. To pokazuje, że rynek nie sprzedawał wszystkiego po równo. Największy ciężar spadł na sektory wrażliwe na wzrost cen ropy i rentowności.
>
> Przemysł i materiały pod presją: Najsłabiej wyglądały spółki przemysłowe i materiałowe. Droższa ropa to wyższe koszty transportu, produkcji i finansowania, więc inwestorzy szybko zaczęli ciąć ekspozycję na bardziej cykliczne segmenty rynku 🏭📉.
>
> Linie lotnicze i rejsy dostają cios: Wzrost cen paliwa uderzył też w spółki turystyczne i transportowe. United Airlines i Delta były pod presją, a operatorzy rejsów, tacy jak Carnival i Norwegian Cruise Line, również mocno traciły ✈️🚢.
>
> Chipy po lepszej stronie rynku: Ciekawie wyglądały półprzewodniki. Broadcom mocno rósł po informacji, że Apple planuje wydać ponad 30 mld USD w ramach umowy dotyczącej dostaw chipów. Nvidia również była na plusie po doniesieniach, że Chiny mogą dopuścić ograniczone zakupy chipów H200 przez największe lokalne firmy AI 🤖💻.
>
> To ważna zmiana po ostatnich dniach nerwowości. AI trade nadal jest chwiejny, ale nie został porzucony. Rynek po prostu coraz ostrzej rozróżnia spółki z konkretnymi kontraktami od tych, które rosną głównie na narracji.
>
> 🌍 Europa: Czerwień na Starym Kontynencie 🇪🇺
> Europa zareagowała na eskalację znacznie słabiej niż GPW. W momencie zamknięcia handlu w Warszawie niemiecki DAX tracił ponad 2%, podobnie słabo wyglądał francuski CAC 40, a brytyjski FTSE 100 spadał o ok. 1,7%.
>
> Warszawa na tym tle była relatywnie mocna. Pomogła struktura WIG20: drożejący Orlen, odbicie banków i popyt na kilka dużych spółek zrównoważyły mocny spadek KGHM. W Europie takiego bufora było mniej 🇪🇺⚖️.
>
> 💱 Waluty, obligacje i Fed: Ropa podbija inflacyjne obawy 💵
> Na rynku długu zrobiło się nerwowo. Rentowność amerykańskich 10-latek wzrosła w okolice 4,56%, a 30-latek przekroczyła 5%. To reakcja na drożejącą ropę i obawy, że kolejny szok energetyczny może utrudnić Fedowi walkę z inflacją.
>
> Do tego doszły minutes z czerwcowego posiedzenia Fedu. Zapiski pokazały podzielony obraz: część członków widzi argumenty za podwyżką stóp, choć na ostatnim posiedzeniu poparła jeszcze utrzymanie ich bez zmian. Rynek dostał więc sygnał, że Fed pod wodzą Kevina Warsha nie zamierza szybko wracać do luźniejszej polityki 🏦.
>
> Dolar zyskiwał na statusie bezpiecznej przystani, a złoty pozostawał pod presją globalnego risk-off. W kraju głównym wydarzeniem była decyzja RPP, ale jej wpływ był ograniczony, bo brak zmiany stóp był szeroko oczekiwany.
>
> 🛢️ Ropa: Geopolityczna premia wraca z impetem ⛽
> Najważniejszy ruch dnia wydarzył się na ropie. Brent rósł w okolice 78-80 USD za baryłkę, a WTI przekraczała 73 USD. Rynek wyceniał ryzyko dalszej eskalacji po amerykańskich uderzeniach na Iran i wypowiedziach Trumpa o końcu porozumienia.
>
> Dodatkowym czynnikiem było cofnięcie licencji pozwalającej Iranowi na globalny eksport ropy. To zwiększyło obawy o dostępność surowca i przypomniało inwestorom, jak wrażliwy pozostaje rynek energii na każdy sygnał z Bliskiego Wschodu 🕊️⚠️.
>
> 💡 Wniosek dnia:
> Środowa sesja była lekcją odporności GPW. Globalnie dominował strach przed eskalacją konfliktu USA-Iran, skokiem cen ropy i powrotem inflacyjnej presji. Europa mocno traciła, Wall Street była pod presją, a rentowności obligacji rosły.
>
> Na tym tle Warszawa zachowała się bardzo solidnie. WIG20 niemal odrobił silną poranną przecenę dzięki Orlenowi, bankom, Allegro i Dino. Z drugiej strony tak głęboki spadek KGHM pokazuje, że rynek pozostaje bardzo selektywny i karze spółki, przy których pojawiają się jednocześnie presja surowcowa oraz obawy o przyszłe wydatki inwestycyjne.
>
> Teraz najważniejsze będą trzy pytania: czy eskalacja wokół Iranu okaże się tylko kolejnym epizodem, czy początkiem większego kryzysu; czy ropa utrzyma się przy wyższych poziomach; oraz jak rynek zinterpretuje bardziej jastrzębie sygnały z Fedu. Jeśli ropa dalej będzie rosła, temat inflacji bardzo szybko wróci na pierwsze strony rynkowej agendy.
>
> #Giełda #WIG20 #GPW #WallStreet #Fed #Iran #Broadcom #Nvidia #FinTwitt #Inwestowanie

### Just2Trade (@Just2Trade)
_Wed Jul 08 19:30:09 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/Just2Trade/status/2074939113703145957)

> 🔬 Hawking Radiation — No Longer Just Theory?
>
> Stephen Hawking predicted that black holes slowly evaporate by emitting radiation — but testing this in space remains impossible. Now, physicists have experimentally studied the *backreaction* of stimulated Hawking radiation using an optical analogue — a lab-based system mimicking a black hole's event horizon with light and fiber optics. This is a landmark step: not just detecting analogue Hawking radiation, but observing how it *affects the system that produced it*. Understanding backreaction is crucial to resolving one of physics' deepest puzzles — the black hole information paradox. Lab-scale black hole mimics are becoming powerful tools for probing quantum gravity.
>
> #HawkingRadiation #QuantumPhysics #BlackHoles #AnalogueGravity #QuantumOptics
>
> ---
>
> Companies in this space: Coherent Corp. ($COHR, NYSE), II-VI / Coherent Advanced Photonics ($IIVI, NASDAQ), MKS Instruments ($MKSI, NASDAQ)

### Signe Plan (@AnetteO11)
_Wed Jul 08 21:35:37 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 1 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/AnetteO11/status/2074970687903563891)

> AMD is not alone or necessarily the first to market in an exclusive way, but they are very much in the race. Ayar Labs has secured major investments, with AMD Ventures, NVIDIA, and Intel Capital all contributing heavy multi-million dollar sums. All three giants are after the same thing: replacing traditional copper cables inside and between AI processors with light signals (optical I/O) to build ultra-fast AI supercomputers.
>
> 2. What is SuperNova?
>
> SuperNova is an external light source (a type of multi-laser device) that sends light across up to 16 different wavelengths through thin fiber-optic cables. Instead of sending electricity through copper, data is transmitted at the speed of light. This provides vastly higher bandwidth, lower latency, and consumes significantly less power, which is exactly what future, massive AI models require.
>
> 3. The Sivers Connection
>
> There is actually an interesting Swedish angle here: it is the semiconductor company Sivers Semiconductors through its subsidiary Sivers Photonics that has developed and delivered the advanced laser arrays used inside Ayar Labs' SuperNova modules.
>
> AMD is at the absolute forefront, integrating this technology into its future chip designs, but they share the pie and the technology with their biggest competitors Nvidia and Intel, who are also deeply involved with Ayar Labs.

### buzzberg.ai (@buzzberg_ai)
_Wed Jul 08 22:59:18 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 0 · [open on X](https://x.com/buzzberg_ai/status/2074991747940118838)

> Daily Buzzberg Alpha
>
> the tape isn't sending one macro signal. it's repricing a regime: geopolitical supply risk returning while ai capex becomes an earnings tailwind AND an inflation/rates risk at the same time.
>
> that combination kills generic beta and creates dispersion. the market has stopped paying for ai exposure or risk-on exposure — it's paying for contracted demand, validated supply-chain position, and balance-sheet capacity. it's punishing crowded trades where the thesis is intact but the holder base is impaired.
>
> the whole note reduces to one filter: contracts > stories.
>
> — where the asymmetry sits —
>
> $WYFI — cleanest setup in the neocloud wreckage. ~$1b+ contracted backlog vs ~$1.3b market cap, and nscale's $900m credit facility validates the counterparty. sold with the basket, priced like the contracts don't exist.
>
> $AVGO — the one ai print this week backed by a signed deal: apple's $30b+ agreement + $1.5b colorado buildout. validates the custom asic layer beyond gpu scarcity. revenue visibility, not vibes — and the cleaner read-through than $AAPL, which carries higher domestic cost and eu overhang.
>
> $ONDS — thesis tied to numbers, not narrative: path to ~$1b revenue by 2027, net-income inflection, sum-of-parts floor, q2 print as the catalyst.
>
> photonics — the under-the-surface one. inp substrates easing from "very tight" to "tight" isn't bearish — it lets downstream optical names convert interconnect demand into shipments. distinguish upstream bottleneck vs downstream qualification moats. $LITE $AAOI $COHR
>
> $RKLB — flow unusually specific: 200dma entry, ms overweight $105 pt, vertical-integration bull case. blue origin's $130b private raise now anchors every public space comp.
>
> — crowded, entry decayed —
>
> $PENG — textbook signal decay. real discovery a month ago (earnings beat, cxl exposure, nvidia ai factory partner). now the flow is victory laps and partial trims. thesis quality high, entry quality gone.
>
> broad ai beta — warsh's divided fomc tied ai capex to upside inflation risk, some members already floating hikes. that's the mechanism: the buildout that feeds suppliers also keeps real rates sticky, so long-duration ai without contract visibility underperforms. $TLT stays exposed.
>
> — battleground —
>
> memory — highest-dispersion area on the tape. korean flow reads the samsung/hynix selloff as forced deleveraging (levered-etf + retail-credit mechanics, adr re-rating catalyst) with hbm4/rubin demand structural through 2028. us flow is chaos — "memory is dead" next to aggressive $MU $SNDK dip buys. right framing: thesis intact, ownership base damaged. tradable, not clean.
>
> oil — the move isn't the crude print, it's the transmission. brent ~$80 is the tactical level where short-covering extends, but the real signal is hormuz uncertainty leaking into diesel, propane, shipping and reserves — inflation pass-through that survives even if front-month crude stalls. own the complex where the physical market stays tight. $USO $CRAK
>
> also on the desk: $NBIS washed-out sub-$170 but the bar is now contracted utilization, $META's $10b canada dc arguing against a capex stop, $OUST physical-ai perception via nvidia jetson, $HOOD chain optionality (early, distribution call not revenue).
>
> bottom line: the tape is moving from "ai trade" to "ai underwriting." it pays receipts and punishes stories — $AVGO and $WYFI have them, $PENG had them last month, memory has them for 2028 but not for this week.

### Dan Coté (@DanCote303)
_Wed Jul 08 23:45:34 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 9 · ↻ 2 · 💬 3 · [open on X](https://x.com/DanCote303/status/2075003388346147121)

> Be warned!! This is a little long but VERY informative on who Kopin should be prospecting and timeline of execution.
>
> I KNOW we are early on $KOPN with its new MicroLED Neural I/o chip design. And its DEMO to be presented end of 2026. So trying to take advantage while their is time, #KOPIN should be looking into hyperscalers first. 
>
> Hyperscalers & Cloud AI Builders (Top Priority)
>
> NVIDIA (GPU clusters, NVLink complements), Google (TPUs), Amazon (Trainium/Inferentia), Microsoft (Azure Maia/custom silicon), Meta, Oracle, xAI, and others building massive AI training/inference clusters.
>
> WHY? 
> They face acute power and bandwidth walls in dense GPU racks. Power/cooling is a top TCO driver; Neural I/o promises major efficiency gains for intra-rack or short inter-rack GPU-to-GPU and GPU-to-memory traffic.
> AI Chip/Accelerator Designers
> NVIDIA, AMD, Broadcom (custom ASICs), and startups (Cerebras, Groq, SambaNova, etc.). Also advanced packaging players (TSMC, Intel, Samsung) for chiplet or co-packaged optics (CPO) integration.
>
> WHY? 
> Direct integration into next-gen accelerators or 2.5D/3D packages. Supports high-parallelism needs without heavy SerDes bottlenecks.
>
> Server/System OEMs & Integrators Supermicro, Dell, HPE, Lenovo.
>
> WHY? 
> They build the racks/servers sold to hyperscalers. Better interconnects enable higher-density, lower-power systems that differentiate their offerings. Networking & Photonics Ecosystem Broadcom (AVGO—networking ASICs/optics leader), Arista, Cisco, plus photonics firms (Lumentum/LITE, Coherent). Potential partners or complementors rather than pure competitors for specific short-reach use cases.
>
> Defense, Government & Sovereign AI Infrastructure
>
> DoD/intelligence community data centers, contractors, and sovereign AI projects (Europe, Middle East, Asia) seeking secure/domestic supply chains.
>
> WHY?
> Kopin’s US-based full MicroLED production capability + long defense heritage (displays, soldier systems) provides a strong moat for secure AI hardware. Dual-use potential with existing defense MicroLED work.
>
> Advantages of $KOPN vs. Current Data Center Interconnects
>
> Neural I/o sits in a “sweet spot” between copper’s limitations and traditional laser optics’ drawbacks for short-to-medium reach, high-bandwidth AI intra-cluster links. It draws from “wide-and-slow” parallel channel concepts (hundreds/thousands of lower-speed MicroLED channels instead of a few ultra-high-speed lanes), similar to Microsoft Research’s MOSAIC project (which demonstrated ~56-68% lower power, up to 50m reach, and much higher reliability using MicroLEDs + imaging fiber).Neural I/o wins on bandwidth scalability (parallelism enables 1.6 Tbps demo target soon, 3.6 Tbps roadmap), dramatically lower power per bit, less heat (easier cooling, higher rack density), and better reach for board/rack scales. It “breaks the copper wall” while keeping costs and power closer to copper-like economics for these reaches.Vs. Traditional Optical (InP/VCSEL lasers, silicon photonics transceivers, pluggable optics or CPO):
> Lasers excel at longer reach but are power-hungry, expensive, thermally sensitive, complex (heavy DSP, CDR, FEC, equalization, SerDes), and overkill (plus higher failure rates) for many short intra-rack or chip-to-chip links in AI clusters. They add cost, power, and complexity where not fully needed.
>
> Neural I/o wins by using MicroLEDs as direct emitters (cheaper, lower power, more temperature-robust, simpler drive electronics possible with parallel low-speed channels). It eliminates or reduces need for expensive laser modules and complex digital backends for targeted use cases. Potential for smaller form factor, higher reliability/redundancy (pixel-level), and better power efficiency (comparable to MOSAIC’s ~3-5W vs. 10-12W per link range in research). Bidirectional capability from NeuralDisplay architecture is a plus. It avoids “expensive laser-based systems entirely” for these applications while delivering needed bandwidth.
>
> LOOONG $KOPN

- https://pbs.twimg.com/media/HMvklTFaoAAvtGp.jpg

> ส่วน AEHR
>
> เพิ่งได้รับคำสั่งซื้อเพิ่มเติมสำหรับระบบ Wafer Level Burn-In (WLBI) จากลูกค้า Silicon Photonics
> มีโอกาสได้รับคำสั่งซื้อเพิ่มภายในปีนี้ หลังผ่านการรับรองเป็นซัพพลายเออร์แล้ว
> ก่อนหน้านี้ยังได้รับคำสั่งซื้อระบบ Package Level Burn-In (PLBI) จากลูกค้า Hyperscaler รายใหญ่
>
> Paradis Labs ระบุว่า หุ้นทั้งสองตัวมีความผันผวนสูง (High Beta) จึงถูกแรงขายในรอบ AI Selloff มากกว่าหุ้นขนาดใหญ่ แต่ยังเชื่อมั่นในแนวโน้มระยะยาวและยังคงถือการลงทุนต่อ

### Mitch (@_MHequities)
_Wed Jul 08 23:55:19 +0000 2026_ · ♥ 0 · ↻ 0 · 💬 2 · [open on X](https://x.com/_MHequities/status/2075005843976630489)

> While AAOI’s primary business is building traditional pluggable optical transceivers, they also develop foundational high-power lasers and external laser sources for CPO architectures. So they’re bridging the gap today while also prepping for what comes next. CPO is a 2028/29 story at best. But the point is having a fundamental basis to justify a stock price today. Whether on a visible discounted cash flow basis or just material revenue/backlog growth TODAY. AAOI has explosive revenue growth actually materializing, on top of a surging **backlog**, whereas Sivers is baiting retail with a merely subjective **opportunity pipeline**, with zero photonics revenue today, let alone even a backlog to show for anything. Just non-exclusive partnerships on reference designs that they hope will be used by 2028. And pricing power will be fully at the discretion of WIN Semi, who they outsource designs to, further eroding potential margins should anything even manifest. I mean hey, this thing could surely pump again, but the risks are IMMENSE and it will only run on hype, which is intrinsically fizzling out (especially with all this dilution and some serious macro risks on the horizon/liquidity tightening). I suspect some funky business going on with their management, and I’m merely trying to make people aware not to blindly follow anonymous pump pages
